### `2026-03-15T02:35:22.052Z`

> <command-message>opsx:archive</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:archive</command-name>

### `2026-03-15T02:35:22.052Z`

> Archive a completed change in the experimental workflow.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:archive` (e.g., `/opsx:archive add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**
> 
>    Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.
> 
>    Show only active changes (not already archived).
>    Include the schema used for each change if available.
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.
> 
> 2. **Check artifact completion status**
> 
>    Run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json` to check artifact completion.
> 
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used
>    - `artifacts`: List of artifacts with their status (`done` or other)
> 
>    **If any artifacts are not `done`:**
>    - Display warning listing incomplete artifacts
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
> 3. **Check task completion status**
> 
>    Read the tasks file (typically `tasks.md`) to check for incomplete tasks.
> 
>    Count tasks marked with `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete).
> 
>    **If incomplete tasks found:**
>    - Display warning showing count of incomplete tasks
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
>    **If no tasks file exists:** Proceed without task-related warning.
> 
> 4. **Assess delta spec sync state**
> 
>    Check for delta specs at `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`. If none exist, proceed without sync prompt.
> 
>    **If delta specs exist:**
>    - Compare each delta spec with its corresponding main spec at `openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md`
>    - Determine what changes would be applied (adds, modifications, removals, renames)
>    - Show a combined summary before prompting
> 
>    **Prompt options:**
>    - If changes needed: "Sync now (recommended)", "Archive without syncing"
>    - If already synced: "Archive now", "Sync anyway", "Cancel"
> 
>    If user chooses sync, use Task tool (subagent_type: "general-purpose", prompt: "Use Skill tool to invoke openspec-sync-specs for change '<name>'. Delta spec analysis: <include the analyzed delta spec summary>"). Proceed to archive regardless of choice.
> 
> 5. **Perform the archive**
> 
>    Create the archive directory if it doesn't exist:
>    ```bash
>    mkdir -p openspec/changes/archive
>    ```
> 
>    Generate target name using current date: `YYYY-MM-DD-<change-name>`
> 
>    **Check if target already exists:**
>    - If yes: Fail with error, suggest renaming existing archive or using different date
>    - If no: Move the change directory to archive
> 
>    ```bash
>    mv openspec/changes/<name> openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>
>    ```
> 
> 6. **Display summary**
> 
>    Show archive completion summary including:
>    - Change name
>    - Schema that was used
>    - Archive location
>    - Spec sync status (synced / sync skipped / no delta specs)
>    - Note about any warnings (incomplete artifacts/tasks)
> 
> **Output On Success**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** ✓ Synced to main specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success (No Delta Specs)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** No delta specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success With Warnings**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete (with warnings)
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** Sync skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> **Warnings:**
> - Archived with 2 incomplete artifacts
> - Archived with 3 incomplete tasks
> - Delta spec sync was skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> Review the archive if this was not intentional.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Error (Archive Exists)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Failed
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Target:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> 
> Target archive directory already exists.
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. Rename the existing archive
> 2. Delete the existing archive if it's a duplicate
> 3. Wait until a different date to archive
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Always prompt for change selection if not provided
> - Use artifact graph (openspec status --json) for completion checking
> - Don't block archive on warnings - just inform and confirm
> - Preserve .openspec.yaml when moving to archive (it moves with the directory)
> - Show clear summary of what happened
> - If sync is requested, use the Skill tool to invoke `openspec-sync-specs` (agent-driven)
> - If delta specs exist, always run the sync assessment and show the combined summary before prompting

>    openspec new change "<name>"
>    ```
>    This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/` with `.openspec.yaml`.
> 
> 3. **Get the artifact build order**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to get:
>    - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
>    - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies
> 
> 4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**
> 
>    Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.
> 
>    Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):
> 
>    a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
>       - Get instructions:
>         ```bash
>         openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
>         ```
>       - The instructions JSON includes:
>         - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
>         - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
>         - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
>         - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
>       - Read any completed dependency files for context
>       - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
>       - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
>       - Show brief progress: "Created <artifact-id>"
> 
>    b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
>       - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
>       - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
>       - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done
> 
>    c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
>       - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
>       - Then continue with creation
> 
> 5. **Show final status**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>"
>    ```
> 
> **Output**
> 
> After completing all artifacts, summarize:
> - Change name and location
> - List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
> - What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
> - Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` to start implementing."
> 
> **Artifact Creation Guidelines**
> 
> - Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
> - The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
> - Read dependency artifacts for context before creating new ones
> - Use `template` as the structure for your output file - fill in its sections
> - **IMPORTANT**: `context` and `rules` are constraints for YOU, not content for the file
>   - Do NOT copy `<context>`, `<rules>`, `<project_context>` blocks into the artifact
>   - These guide what you write, but should never appear in the output
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
> - Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
> - If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
> - If a change with that name already exists, ask if user wants to continue it or create a new one
> - Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next
>

### `2026-03-15T02:56:42.467Z`

> <task-notification>
> <task-id>a0a2273b190ed1e98</task-id>
> <tool-use-id>toolu_017MiVJ5hvzPfkooPo1tb139</tool-use-id>
> <output-file>/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-lane-src-lin-pane/0c91add2-2144-48f1-bd01-bf47fe72e9f3/tasks/a0a2273b190ed1e98.output</output-file>

> <summary>Agent "Review pane-proto codebase" completed</summary>
> <result>Reviewing the pane-proto crate. All files read. Here is the full analysis.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Critical
> 
> ### 1. `frame` can silently truncate on payloads >= 4 GiB (confidence: 85)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/wire.rs`, line 15
> 
> ```rust
> let len = payload.len() as u32;
> ```
> 
> `payload.len()` returns `usize`. On a 64-bit target, `usize` is 64 bits. The cast to `u32` is silent truncation — no panic, no error, just a corrupt length prefix. The downstream reader will try to read `len & 0xFFFFFFFF` bytes and either underread or block forever.
> 
> In practice a 4 GiB frame is impossible for this protocol, but the function takes `&[u8]` with no stated bound, so it is silently wrong for any input >= 4 GiB and the caller gets no signal.
> 
> Concrete fix: either assert or return an error.
> 
> ```rust
> pub fn frame(payload: &[u8]) -> Result<Vec<u8>, postcard::Error> {
>     let len: u32 = payload.len().try_into()
>         .map_err(|_| postcard::Error::SerializeBufferFull)?;
>     ...
> }
> ```
> 
> Or if you want to keep the infallible signature, add `assert!(payload.len() <= u32::MAX as usize)`. Either way, make the constraint explicit.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. State machine: `Disconnected` reconnect is silently swallowed (confidence: 90)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/state.rs`, line 92–96
> 
> ```rust
> pub fn connect(&self) -> Result<ProtocolState, ProtocolError> {
>     match self {
>         ProtocolState::Disconnected => Ok(ProtocolState::Connected),
>         _ => Ok(self.clone()),  // ← silently succeeds from Active or Connected
>     }
> }
> ```
> 
> Calling `connect()` on an already-`Active` or `Connected` state returns `Ok` with no state change. The error type has `NotConnected` but no `AlreadyConnected`. This means a client that accidentally calls `connect()` twice (e.g. a reconnect path) will get `Ok` and incorrectly believe a fresh handshake occurred, while actually still sitting in `Active` with an existing pane. That's a protocol logic error that will manifest as the compositor seeing a `Create` when it expects pane-scoped requests.
> 
> Fix: either make `connect()` idempotent by design (document it) and rename to `ensure_connected`, or return an error on double-connect.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. State machine: `apply(Create)` on `Connected` does not advance state — `activate` call is mandatory but unenforceable (confidence: 80)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/state.rs`, line 55–60
> 
> ```rust
> (ProtocolState::Connected, PaneRequest::Create { .. }) => {
>     Ok(ProtocolState::Connected)  // stays Connected
> }
> ```
> 
> The comment says "we stay Connected until we see the response." Fine — but nothing in the type system or the API enforces that the caller must call `activate()` before sending another request. If the client fires a second `Create` between the first `Create` and the compositor's `Created` response, `apply` returns `Ok(Connected)` again instead of erroring. The compositor will receive two `Create` messages while the client's state machine thinks only one was sent.
> 
> This is a design gap. Options in increasing robustness:
> - Add a `PendingCreate` state that is entered after `apply(Create)` returns `Ok` and is the only state from which `activate()` transitions to `Active`.
> - Or detect it by tracking that a create is in-flight (a bool on the state) and reject a second `Create` while one is outstanding.
> 
> The current design makes the protocol correct only if the caller is disciplined, but the state machine's stated purpose is to prevent exactly this class of mistake.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Important
> 
> ### 4. `CellRegion` has no height field and allows incoherent `cells` lengths (confidence: 85)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/cell.rs`, line 42–51
> 
> `CellRegion` stores `col`, `row`, `width`, and `cells: Vec<Cell>`, but no `height`. The intended layout is row-major, so `cells.len()` must be a multiple of `width` for the region to tile correctly. Nothing enforces this. A `CellRegion` with `width: 3` and `cells.len(): 7` is representable, valid to serialize, will round-trip cleanly, and will corrupt the compositor's cell grid when written.
> 
> The comment says "cells in row-major order" but `height = cells.len() / width` is implicit and only recoverable if `cells.len() % width == 0`, which is not checked.
> 
> Fix: either add a `height: u16` field (explicit and checkable) or add a constructor that validates and a `height()` accessor that asserts divisibility. Given this is a wire type, explicit `height` is safer — the compositor can validate `cells.len() == width as usize * height as usize` on receipt.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 5. `WriteCells` with `Surface` pane kind is semantically nonsensical but accepted (confidence: 80)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/message.rs`, lines 40, 28–29
> 
> `PaneKind::Surface` means the client renders pixels. `PaneRequest::WriteCells` is cell-grid data. The protocol does not distinguish: a client can send `WriteCells` to a `Surface` pane, and `apply()` will return `Ok`. The compositor will receive it and either discard it silently or misinterpret it.
> 
> Since the compositor assigns the id, it knows the kind — but the client-side state machine doesn't track kind, so it cannot reject this. The fix is to track `PaneKind` in `ProtocolState::Active`:
> 
> ```rust
> Active { pane_id: PaneId, kind: PaneKind }
> ```
> 
> and reject `WriteCells` / `Scroll` / `SetDirty` when `kind == Surface`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 6. `PaneId::new` is public — the "only the compositor should call this" doc comment is not enforced (confidence: 80)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/message.rs`, line 14
> 
> ```rust
> /// Create a PaneId. Only the compositor should call this.
> pub fn new(id: NonZeroU32) -> Self {
> ```
> 
> This is a crate that is shared between client and compositor. A client can construct arbitrary `PaneId` values and send them. The state machine's `WrongPaneId` check is the only defense, but once the client is `Active`, it knows the `pane_id` and can construct matching ids trivially anyway. The intent seems to be preventing the client from forging ids in a multi-pane future — but the current single-active-pane design makes that gap acute.
> 
> If the intent is to restrict construction to the compositor side, the fix is to gate this behind a feature flag (e.g., `compositor` feature) or put it in a separate `pane-proto-compositor` crate. If the crate is internal-only and trust is assumed, the doc comment is the right call — but it should say so explicitly.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 7. `NamedKey::F(u8)` range is unbounded — `F(0)` and `F(255)` are representable (confidence: 82)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/event.rs`, line 38
> 
> `F(u8)` can hold any value 0–255. Conventional function keys are F1–F24 at most (some systems go to F35). `F(0)` is meaningless and `F(200)` will silently be accepted, serialized, round-tripped, and presumably passed to whatever keybinding system consumes these.
> 
> The roundtrip test generates `1..=12u8` for `F`, so the test does not cover the out-of-range values. This is a minor mismatch between wire type and test, but the core issue is that the wire type is too permissive.
> 
> Options: use a newtype with a `TryFrom<u8>` that validates range, or document the accepted range and validate on receipt. The roundtrip test should at minimum cover the full `u8` range if `F(u8)` is the intended representation.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Minor
> 
> ### 8. `frame` and `frame_length` are not exported from `lib.rs` (confidence: 82)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/lib.rs`, line 13
> 
> ```rust
> pub use wire::{deserialize, serialize};
> ```
> 
> `frame` and `frame_length` are defined in `wire.rs` with `pub` visibility but are not re-exported from the crate root. Any code that uses `pane_proto::frame` will fail to compile unless it imports `pane_proto::wire::frame` directly — which leaks the internal module structure. Either re-export them or make the function-level visibility match the export decision.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 9. `ProtocolState` derives `Serialize`/`Deserialize` but there is no stated use for that (confidence: 80)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/state.rs`, line 8
> 
> State machine state is not a wire type — it is local per-connection tracking. Deriving `Serialize`/`Deserialize` on it suggests it might be sent on the wire or persisted, which would be a design smell (sharing state machine state between client and compositor couples them). If it is only for testing convenience, use `#[cfg_attr(test, derive(Serialize, Deserialize))]`. If there is a real use case for serializing it, document it.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 10. `Scroll` delta direction is undocumented (confidence: 80)
> 
> **File:** `/Users/lane/src/lin/pane/crates/pane-proto/src/message.rs`, line 42
> 
> ```rust
> Scroll { id: PaneId, delta: i32 },
> ```
> 
> No doc comment specifies the sign convention (positive = scroll down? scroll up?), the unit (rows? pixels? lines?), or the maximum meaningful range. This will produce bugs when the compositor and client independently choose a convention. Doc comment minimum: `/// delta > 0 scrolls down (toward newer content) by that many rows`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Summary
> 
> | # | Severity | Area | One-liner |
> |---|----------|------|-----------|
> | 1 | Critical | wire.rs | `as u32` truncation in `frame()` |
> | 2 | Critical | state.rs | `connect()` silently succeeds when already Active |
> | 3 | Critical | state.rs | Double-Create between request and `activate()` not rejected |
> | 4 | Important | cell.rs | `CellRegion` missing `height`, incoherent cell count undetectable |
> | 5 | Important | message.rs + state.rs | `WriteCells` accepted for `Surface` panes |
> | 6 | Important | message.rs | `PaneId::new` is pub, doc intent not enforced |
> | 7 | Important | event.rs | `NamedKey::F(u8)` accepts garbage values |
> | 8 | Minor | lib.rs | `frame`/`frame_length` not re-exported |
> | 9 | Minor | state.rs | `ProtocolState` serialization rationale unstated |
> | 10 | Minor | message.rs | `Scroll::delta` sign/unit convention undocumented |
> 
> The most structurally important fix is #3 (add `PendingCreate` state) — the current two-step `apply(Create)` + `activate()` split creates a correctness gap that the state machine exists to prevent. Issues #4 and #5 both point at the same root cause: `ProtocolState::Active` doesn't track `PaneKind`, and `CellRegion` has no explicit height, so the compositor is doing implicit recovery work that the wire type should do for it.</result>

### `2026-03-15T05:16:58.994Z`

> Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name (e.g., `/opsx:apply add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **Select the change**
> 
>    If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
>    - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
>    - Auto-select if only one active change exists
>    - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select
> 
>    Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).
> 
> 2. **Check status to understand the schema**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
>    - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)
> 
> 3. **Get apply instructions**
> 
>    ```bash
>    openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
> 
>    This returns:
>    - Context file paths (varies by schema)
>    - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
>    - Task list with status
>    - Dynamic instruction based on current state
> 
>    **Handle states:**
>    - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using `/opsx:continue`
>    - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
>    - Otherwise: proceed to implementation
> 
> 4. **Read context files**
> 
>    Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
>    The files depend on the schema being used:
>    - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
>    - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output
> 
> 5. **Show current progress**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Schema being used
>    - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - Remaining tasks overview
>    - Dynamic instruction from CLI
> 
> 6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**
> 
>    For each pending task:
>    - Show which task is being worked on
>    - Make the code changes required
>    - Keep changes minimal and focused
>    - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
>    - Continue to next task
> 
>    **Pause if:**
>    - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
>    - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
>    - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
>    - User interrupts
> 
> 7. **On completion or pause, show status**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Tasks completed this session
>    - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - If all done: suggest archive
>    - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance
> 
> **Output During Implementation**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementing: <change-name> (schema: <schema-name>)
> 
> Working on task 3/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> 
> Working on task 4/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> ```
> 
> **Output On Completion**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 7/7 tasks complete ✓
> 
> ### Completed This Session
> - [x] Task 1
> - [x] Task 2
> ...
> 
> All tasks complete! You can archive this change with `/opsx:archive`.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Pause (Issue Encountered)**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Paused
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 4/7 tasks complete
> 
> ### Issue Encountered
> <description of the issue>
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. <option 1>
> 2. <option 2>
> 3. Other approach
> 
> What would you like to do?
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Keep going through tasks until done or blocked
> - Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
> - If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
> - If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
> - Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
> - Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
> - Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
> - Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names
> 
> **Fluid Workflow Integration**
> 
> This skill supports the "actions on a change" model:
> 
> - **Can be invoked anytime**: Before all artifacts are done (if tasks exist), after partial implementation, interleaved with other actions
> - **Allows artifact updates**: If implementation reveals design issues, suggest updating artifacts - not phase-locked, work fluidly

### `2026-03-15T06:04:01.744Z`

> Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name (e.g., `/opsx:apply add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **Select the change**
> 
>    If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
>    - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
>    - Auto-select if only one active change exists
>    - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select
> 
>    Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).
> 
> 2. **Check status to understand the schema**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
>    - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)
> 
> 3. **Get apply instructions**
> 
>    ```bash
>    openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
> 
>    This returns:
>    - Context file paths (varies by schema)
>    - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
>    - Task list with status
>    - Dynamic instruction based on current state
> 
>    **Handle states:**
>    - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using `/opsx:continue`
>    - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
>    - Otherwise: proceed to implementation
> 
> 4. **Read context files**
> 
>    Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
>    The files depend on the schema being used:
>    - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
>    - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output
> 
> 5. **Show current progress**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Schema being used
>    - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - Remaining tasks overview
>    - Dynamic instruction from CLI
> 
> 6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**
> 
>    For each pending task:
>    - Show which task is being worked on
>    - Make the code changes required
>    - Keep changes minimal and focused
>    - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
>    - Continue to next task
> 
>    **Pause if:**
>    - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
>    - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
>    - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
>    - User interrupts
> 
> 7. **On completion or pause, show status**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Tasks completed this session
>    - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - If all done: suggest archive
>    - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance
> 
> **Output During Implementation**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementing: <change-name> (schema: <schema-name>)
> 
> Working on task 3/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> 
> Working on task 4/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> ```
> 
> **Output On Completion**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 7/7 tasks complete ✓
> 
> ### Completed This Session
> - [x] Task 1
> - [x] Task 2
> ...
> 
> All tasks complete! You can archive this change with `/opsx:archive`.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Pause (Issue Encountered)**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Paused
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 4/7 tasks complete
> 
> ### Issue Encountered
> <description of the issue>
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. <option 1>
> 2. <option 2>
> 3. Other approach
> 
> What would you like to do?
> ```
>

### `2026-03-15T07:40:38.223Z`

> <command-message>opsx:archive</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:archive</command-name>

### `2026-03-15T07:40:38.223Z`

> Archive a completed change in the experimental workflow.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:archive` (e.g., `/opsx:archive add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**
> 
>    Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.
> 
>    Show only active changes (not already archived).
>    Include the schema used for each change if available.
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.
> 
> 2. **Check artifact completion status**
> 
>    Run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json` to check artifact completion.
> 
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used
>    - `artifacts`: List of artifacts with their status (`done` or other)
> 
>    **If any artifacts are not `done`:**
>    - Display warning listing incomplete artifacts
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
> 3. **Check task completion status**
> 
>    Read the tasks file (typically `tasks.md`) to check for incomplete tasks.
> 
>    Count tasks marked with `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete).
> 
>    **If incomplete tasks found:**
>    - Display warning showing count of incomplete tasks
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
>    **If no tasks file exists:** Proceed without task-related warning.
> 
> 4. **Assess delta spec sync state**
> 
>    Check for delta specs at `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`. If none exist, proceed without sync prompt.
> 
>    **If delta specs exist:**
>    - Compare each delta spec with its corresponding main spec at `openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md`
>    - Determine what changes would be applied (adds, modifications, removals, renames)
>    - Show a combined summary before prompting
> 
>    **Prompt options:**
>    - If changes needed: "Sync now (recommended)", "Archive without syncing"
>    - If already synced: "Archive now", "Sync anyway", "Cancel"
> 
>    If user chooses sync, use Task tool (subagent_type: "general-purpose", prompt: "Use Skill tool to invoke openspec-sync-specs for change '<name>'. Delta spec analysis: <include the analyzed delta spec summary>"). Proceed to archive regardless of choice.
> 
> 5. **Perform the archive**
> 
>    Create the archive directory if it doesn't exist:
>    ```bash
>    mkdir -p openspec/changes/archive
>    ```
> 
>    Generate target name using current date: `YYYY-MM-DD-<change-name>`
> 
>    **Check if target already exists:**
>    - If yes: Fail with error, suggest renaming existing archive or using different date
>    - If no: Move the change directory to archive
> 
>    ```bash
>    mv openspec/changes/<name> openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>
>    ```
> 
> 6. **Display summary**
> 
>    Show archive completion summary including:
>    - Change name
>    - Schema that was used
>    - Archive location
>    - Spec sync status (synced / sync skipped / no delta specs)
>    - Note about any warnings (incomplete artifacts/tasks)
> 
> **Output On Success**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** ✓ Synced to main specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success (No Delta Specs)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** No delta specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success With Warnings**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete (with warnings)
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** Sync skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> **Warnings:**
> - Archived with 2 incomplete artifacts
> - Archived with 3 incomplete tasks
> - Delta spec sync was skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> Review the archive if this was not intentional.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Error (Archive Exists)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Failed
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Target:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> 
> Target archive directory already exists.
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. Rename the existing archive
> 2. Delete the existing archive if it's a duplicate
> 3. Wait until a different date to archive
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Always prompt for change selection if not provided
> - Use artifact graph (openspec status --json) for completion checking
> - Don't block archive on warnings - just inform and confirm
> - Preserve .openspec.yaml when moving to archive (it moves with the directory)
> - Show clear summary of what happened
> - If sync is requested, use the Skill tool to invoke `openspec-sync-specs` (agent-driven)
> - If delta specs exist, always run the sync assessment and show the combined summary before prompting

### `2026-03-15T07:46:52.057Z`

> <command-message>opsx:propose</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:propose</command-name>

### `2026-03-15T07:46:52.057Z`

> Propose a new change - create the change and generate all artifacts in one step.
> 
> I'll create a change with artifacts:
> - proposal.md (what & why)
> - design.md (how)
> - tasks.md (implementation steps)
> 
> When ready to implement, run /opsx:apply
> 
> ---
> 
> **Input**: The argument after `/opsx:propose` is the change name (kebab-case), OR a description of what the user wants to build.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no input provided, ask what they want to build**
> 
>    Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** (open-ended, no preset options) to ask:
>    > "What change do you want to work on? Describe what you want to build or fix."
> 
>    From their description, derive a kebab-case name (e.g., "add user authentication" → `add-user-auth`).
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT proceed without understanding what the user wants to build.
> 
> 2. **Create the change directory**
>    ```bash
>    openspec new change "<name>"
>    ```
>    This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/` with `.openspec.yaml`.
> 
> 3. **Get the artifact build order**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to get:
>    - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
>    - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies
> 
> 4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**
> 
>    Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.
> 
>    Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):
> 
>    a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
>       - Get instructions:
>         ```bash
>         openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
>         ```
>       - The instructions JSON includes:
>         - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
>         - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
>         - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
>         - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
>       - Read any completed dependency files for context
>       - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
>       - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
>       - Show brief progress: "Created <artifact-id>"
> 
>    b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
>       - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
>       - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
>       - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done
> 
>    c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
>       - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
>       - Then continue with creation
> 
> 5. **Show final status**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>"
>    ```
> 
> **Output**
> 
> After completing all artifacts, summarize:
> - Change name and location
> - List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
> - What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
> - Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` to start implementing."
> 
> **Artifact Creation Guidelines**
> 
> - Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
> - The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
> - Read dependency artifacts for context before creating new ones
> - Use `template` as the structure for your output file - fill in its sections
> - **IMPORTANT**: `context` and `rules` are constraints for YOU, not content for the file
>   - Do NOT copy `<context>`, `<rules>`, `<project_context>` blocks into the artifact
>   - These guide what you write, but should never appear in the output
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
> - Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
> - If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
> - If a change with that name already exists, ask if user wants to continue it or create a new one
> - Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next

### `2026-03-15T07:47:01.381Z`

> <command-message>opsx:apply</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:apply</command-name>

### `2026-03-15T07:47:01.381Z`

> Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name (e.g., `/opsx:apply add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **Select the change**
> 
>    If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
>    - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
>    - Auto-select if only one active change exists
>    - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select
> 
>    Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).
> 
> 2. **Check status to understand the schema**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
>    - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)
> 
> 3. **Get apply instructions**
> 
>    ```bash
>    openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
> 
>    This returns:
>    - Context file paths (varies by schema)
>    - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
>    - Task list with status
>    - Dynamic instruction based on current state
> 
>    **Handle states:**
>    - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using `/opsx:continue`
>    - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
>    - Otherwise: proceed to implementation
> 
> 4. **Read context files**
> 
>    Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
>    The files depend on the schema being used:
>    - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
>    - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output
> 
> 5. **Show current progress**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Schema being used
>    - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - Remaining tasks overview
>    - Dynamic instruction from CLI
> 
> 6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**
> 
>    For each pending task:
>    - Show which task is being worked on
>    - Make the code changes required
>    - Keep changes minimal and focused
>    - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
>    - Continue to next task
> 
>    **Pause if:**
>    - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
>    - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
>    - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
>    - User interrupts
> 
> 7. **On completion or pause, show status**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Tasks completed this session
>    - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - If all done: suggest archive
>    - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance
> 
> **Output During Implementation**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementing: <change-name> (schema: <schema-name>)
> 
> Working on task 3/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> 
> Working on task 4/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> ```
> 
> **Output On Completion**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 7/7 tasks complete ✓
> 
> ### Completed This Session
> - [x] Task 1
> - [x] Task 2
> ...
> 
> All tasks complete! You can archive this change with `/opsx:archive`.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Pause (Issue Encountered)**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Paused
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 4/7 tasks complete
> 
> ### Issue Encountered
> <description of the issue>
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. <option 1>
> 2. <option 2>
> 3. Other approach
> 
> What would you like to do?
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Keep going through tasks until done or blocked
> - Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
> - If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
> - If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
> - Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
> - Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
> - Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
> - Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names
> 
> **Fluid Workflow Integration**
> 
> This skill supports the "actions on a change" model:
> 
> - **Can be invoked anytime**: Before all artifacts are done (if tasks exist), after partial implementation, interleaved with other actions
> - **Allows artifact updates**: If implementation reveals design issues, suggest updating artifacts - not phase-locked, work fluidly

### `2026-03-15T17:07:02.327Z`

> does nix-darwin have qemu or do I need to install it through breww?

### `2026-03-15T17:58:49.597Z`

> can you answer these questions
> 
> ```
> 
>   I'm setting up a QEMU-based testing workflow on aarch64-darwin (macOS, Apple Silicon) to run your Linux DE
>   in a VM with HVF acceleration. To configure the VM optimally, I need to understand:
> 
>   1. Display protocol — Is the DE targeting Wayland, X11, or both? This determines whether we need virtio-gpu
>    with Wayland-native output or need to wire up Xwayland/X11 forwarding.
>   2. GPU/rendering requirements — Does the DE need OpenGL/Vulkan contexts, or is it software-rendered / 2D
>   only? virtio-gpu supports virgl for OpenGL passthrough, but it has limitations — need to know what the
>   compositor expects.
>   3. Resolution and display scaling — What resolution(s) should the VM present? Any HiDPI/scaling
>   requirements? This affects the -device virtio-gpu-pci,xres=...,yres=... config.
>   4. Audio — Does the DE have audio components that need testing? If so, I'll wire in CoreAudio passthrough
>   (-audiodev coreaudio).
>   5. Base image/distro — What Linux distribution and image format (.qcow2, .img, raw)? Is this a NixOS image,
>    a custom initramfs, or something else? This affects boot chain and firmware config.
>   6. Iteration workflow — How do you want to push DE changes into the VM? Options:
>     - Shared directory via virtio-9p/virtiofs (mount host folder in guest, edit on host, test in guest)
>     - Rebuild image each cycle
>     - SSH in and rsync
> 
>   This is the biggest workflow impact — the right answer here saves minutes per iteration.
>   7. Networking needs — Just outbound internet (install packages), or do you need host↔guest communication
>   (e.g., SSH into the VM, forward a port)?
>   8. Input devices — Keyboard and mouse/touchpad are wired. Anything else? Touchscreen emulation, gamepad,
>   etc.?
> ```

### `2026-03-15T18:08:02.526Z`

> here is the response:

### `2026-03-15T18:08:03.376Z`

> [interrupted]

### `2026-03-15T18:08:10.748Z`

> here is the response:
> 
> ```
> ⏺ ★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────
>   - virtio-gpu-gl-pci vs virtio-gpu-pci — the -gl- variant enables virgl, which translates guest OpenGL/GLES
>   calls to host GL. This is what smithay's renderer_glow (GLES) needs for hardware-accelerated rendering in
>   the guest.
>   - -display cocoa,gl=on — gives the host display backend a GL context, which virgl needs to actually pass
>   through the rendering.
>   - hostfwd=tcp::2222-:22 — maps host port 2222 to guest port 22, so ssh -p 2222 localhost gets you into the
>   VM for debugging.
>   ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
> 
>   Changes from the answers:
>   - virtio-gpu-gl-pci with 1280x720 for virgl + GLES passthrough
>   - gl=on on the cocoa display to back virgl
>   - SSH port forward on 2222
>   - No audio devices (removed from consideration)
> 
>   One caveat: virgl on macOS is not guaranteed — nixpkgs may not compile QEMU with virgl support on darwin,
>   since it depends on virglrenderer which historically targets Linux. If virtio-gpu-gl-pci isn't recognized
>   at runtime, the fallback is swapping back to virtio-gpu-pci and relying on llvmpipe in the guest — which
>   should be fine given pane-comp's rendering load is light 2D.
> 
>   Usage:
>   # Boot the NixOS VM image
>   qemu-vm -drive file=result/nixos.qcow2,format=qcow2
> 
>   # SSH in for debugging
>   ssh -p 2222 localhost
> ```

### `2026-03-15T18:32:46.488Z`

> I have qemu in my environment with these settings, perhaps we adapt:
> 
> ```
>  -M virt — ARM virtual machine type, paravirt only
>   - -accel hvf — Apple Hypervisor.framework for near-native speed
>   - -cpu host — pass through Apple Silicon CPU model
>   - -smp 4 — 4 virtual CPU cores
>   - -m 4G — 4 GB RAM
>   - -device virtio-gpu-gl-pci,xres=1280,yres=720 — paravirt GPU with virgl OpenGL passthrough at 720p
>   - -display cocoa,gl=on — native macOS window with GL context for virgl
>   - -device qemu-xhci — USB 3.0 host controller
>   - -device usb-kbd — USB keyboard
>   - -device usb-tablet — USB tablet, absolute positioning (no mouse grab)
>   - -nic user,model=virtio-net-pci,hostfwd=tcp::2222-:22 — usermode networking with virtio NIC, SSH on host
>   port 2222
>   - -bios .../edk2-aarch64-code.fd — UEFI firmware (required, virt has no legacy BIOS)
> ```

### `2026-03-15T20:18:37.214Z`

> "  The cell grid renderer. We just saw it — fighting smithay's API for basic quad rendering. smithay is
>   designed for compositors that composite Wayland surfaces, not for compositors that render their own cell
>   grids. We're using it against the grain. The glyph atlas → textured quad pipeline is straightforward in raw
>    OpenGL but awkward through smithay's Frame abstraction. I think we'll end up needing a thin custom GL
>   layer for text rendering, using smithay only for the Wayland protocol handling and surface compositing
>   (legacy clients). That's a design decision we'll face soon." we need to think about this, yes

### `2026-03-15T20:39:13.428Z`

> Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name (e.g., `/opsx:apply add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **Select the change**
> 
>    If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
>    - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
>    - Auto-select if only one active change exists
>    - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select
> 
>    Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).
> 
> 2. **Check status to understand the schema**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
>    - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)
> 
> 3. **Get apply instructions**
> 
>    ```bash
>    openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
> 
>    This returns:
>    - Context file paths (varies by schema)
>    - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
>    - Task list with status
>    - Dynamic instruction based on current state
> 
>    **Handle states:**
>    - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using `/opsx:continue`
>    - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
>    - Otherwise: proceed to implementation
> 
> 4. **Read context files**
> 
>    Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
>    The files depend on the schema being used:
>    - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
>    - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output
> 
> 5. **Show current progress**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Schema being used
>    - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - Remaining tasks overview
>    - Dynamic instruction from CLI
> 
> 6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**
> 
>    For each pending task:
>    - Show which task is being worked on
>    - Make the code changes required
>    - Keep changes minimal and focused
>    - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
>    - Continue to next task
> 
>    **Pause if:**
>    - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
>    - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
>    - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
>    - User interrupts
> 
> 7. **On completion or pause, show status**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Tasks completed this session
>    - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - If all done: suggest archive
>    - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance
> 
> **Output During Implementation**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementing: <change-name> (schema: <schema-name>)
> 
> Working on task 3/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> 
> Working on task 4/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> ```
> 
> **Output On Completion**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 7/7 tasks complete ✓
> 
> ### Completed This Session
> - [x] Task 1
> - [x] Task 2
> ...
> 
> All tasks complete! You can archive this change with `/opsx:archive`.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Pause (Issue Encountered)**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Paused
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 4/7 tasks complete
> 
> ### Issue Encountered
> <description of the issue>
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. <option 1>
> 2. <option 2>
> 3. Other approach
> 
> What would you like to do?
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Keep going through tasks until done or blocked
> - Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
> - If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
> - If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
> - Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
> - Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
> - Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
> - Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names
> 
> **Fluid Workflow Integration**
> 
> This skill supports the "actions on a change" model:
> 
> - **Can be invoked anytime**: Before all artifacts are done (if tasks exist), after partial implementation, interleaved with other actions
> - **Allows artifact updates**: If implementation reveals design issues, suggest updating artifacts - not phase-locked, work fluidly
> 
> 
> ARGUMENTS: widget-kit-and-aesthetic

### `2026-03-16T17:35:51.800Z`

> <command-message>opsx:archive</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:archive</command-name>

### `2026-03-16T17:35:51.800Z`

> Archive a completed change in the experimental workflow.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:archive` (e.g., `/opsx:archive add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**
> 
>    Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.
> 
>    Show only active changes (not already archived).
>    Include the schema used for each change if available.
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.
> 
> 2. **Check artifact completion status**
> 
>    Run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json` to check artifact completion.
> 
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used
>    - `artifacts`: List of artifacts with their status (`done` or other)
> 
>    **If any artifacts are not `done`:**
>    - Display warning listing incomplete artifacts
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
> 3. **Check task completion status**
> 
>    Read the tasks file (typically `tasks.md`) to check for incomplete tasks.
> 
>    Count tasks marked with `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete).
> 
>    **If incomplete tasks found:**
>    - Display warning showing count of incomplete tasks
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
>    **If no tasks file exists:** Proceed without task-related warning.
> 
> 4. **Assess delta spec sync state**
> 
>    Check for delta specs at `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`. If none exist, proceed without sync prompt.
> 
>    **If delta specs exist:**
>    - Compare each delta spec with its corresponding main spec at `openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md`
>    - Determine what changes would be applied (adds, modifications, removals, renames)
>    - Show a combined summary before prompting
> 
>    **Prompt options:**
>    - If changes needed: "Sync now (recommended)", "Archive without syncing"
>    - If already synced: "Archive now", "Sync anyway", "Cancel"
> 
>    If user chooses sync, use Task tool (subagent_type: "general-purpose", prompt: "Use Skill tool to invoke openspec-sync-specs for change '<name>'. Delta spec analysis: <include the analyzed delta spec summary>"). Proceed to archive regardless of choice.
> 
> 5. **Perform the archive**
> 
>    Create the archive directory if it doesn't exist:
>    ```bash
>    mkdir -p openspec/changes/archive
>    ```
> 
>    Generate target name using current date: `YYYY-MM-DD-<change-name>`
> 
>    **Check if target already exists:**
>    - If yes: Fail with error, suggest renaming existing archive or using different date
>    - If no: Move the change directory to archive
> 
>    ```bash
>    mv openspec/changes/<name> openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>
>    ```
> 
> 6. **Display summary**
> 
>    Show archive completion summary including:
>    - Change name
>    - Schema that was used
>    - Archive location
>    - Spec sync status (synced / sync skipped / no delta specs)
>    - Note about any warnings (incomplete artifacts/tasks)
> 
> **Output On Success**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** ✓ Synced to main specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success (No Delta Specs)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** No delta specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success With Warnings**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete (with warnings)
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** Sync skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> **Warnings:**
> - Archived with 2 incomplete artifacts
> - Archived with 3 incomplete tasks
> - Delta spec sync was skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> Review the archive if this was not intentional.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Error (Archive Exists)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Failed
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Target:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> 
> Target archive directory already exists.
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. Rename the existing archive
> 2. Delete the existing archive if it's a duplicate
> 3. Wait until a different date to archive
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Always prompt for change selection if not provided
> - Use artifact graph (openspec status --json) for completion checking
> - Don't block archive on warnings - just inform and confirm
> - Preserve .openspec.yaml when moving to archive (it moves with the directory)
> - Show clear summary of what happened
> - If sync is requested, use the Skill tool to invoke `openspec-sync-specs` (agent-driven)
> - If delta specs exist, always run the sync assessment and show the combined summary before prompting

### `2026-03-16T17:36:22.998Z`

> <command-message>opsx:apply</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:apply</command-name>

### `2026-03-16T17:36:22.998Z`

> Implement tasks from an OpenSpec change.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name (e.g., `/opsx:apply add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **Select the change**
> 
>    If a name is provided, use it. Otherwise:
>    - Infer from conversation context if the user mentioned a change
>    - Auto-select if only one active change exists
>    - If ambiguous, run `openspec list --json` to get available changes and use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select
> 
>    Always announce: "Using change: <name>" and how to override (e.g., `/opsx:apply <other>`).
> 
> 2. **Check status to understand the schema**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
>    - Which artifact contains the tasks (typically "tasks" for spec-driven, check status for others)
> 
> 3. **Get apply instructions**
> 
>    ```bash
>    openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
> 
>    This returns:
>    - Context file paths (varies by schema)
>    - Progress (total, complete, remaining)
>    - Task list with status
>    - Dynamic instruction based on current state
> 
>    **Handle states:**
>    - If `state: "blocked"` (missing artifacts): show message, suggest using `/opsx:continue`
>    - If `state: "all_done"`: congratulate, suggest archive
>    - Otherwise: proceed to implementation
> 
> 4. **Read context files**
> 
>    Read the files listed in `contextFiles` from the apply instructions output.
>    The files depend on the schema being used:
>    - **spec-driven**: proposal, specs, design, tasks
>    - Other schemas: follow the contextFiles from CLI output
> 
> 5. **Show current progress**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Schema being used
>    - Progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - Remaining tasks overview
>    - Dynamic instruction from CLI
> 
> 6. **Implement tasks (loop until done or blocked)**
> 
>    For each pending task:
>    - Show which task is being worked on
>    - Make the code changes required
>    - Keep changes minimal and focused
>    - Mark task complete in the tasks file: `- [ ]` → `- [x]`
>    - Continue to next task
> 
>    **Pause if:**
>    - Task is unclear → ask for clarification
>    - Implementation reveals a design issue → suggest updating artifacts
>    - Error or blocker encountered → report and wait for guidance
>    - User interrupts
> 
> 7. **On completion or pause, show status**
> 
>    Display:
>    - Tasks completed this session
>    - Overall progress: "N/M tasks complete"
>    - If all done: suggest archive
>    - If paused: explain why and wait for guidance
> 
> **Output During Implementation**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementing: <change-name> (schema: <schema-name>)
> 
> Working on task 3/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> 
> Working on task 4/7: <task description>
> [...implementation happening...]
> ✓ Task complete
> ```
> 
> **Output On Completion**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 7/7 tasks complete ✓
> 
> ### Completed This Session
> - [x] Task 1
> - [x] Task 2
> ...
> 
> All tasks complete! You can archive this change with `/opsx:archive`.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Pause (Issue Encountered)**
> 
> ```
> ## Implementation Paused
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Progress:** 4/7 tasks complete
> 
> ### Issue Encountered
> <description of the issue>
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. <option 1>
> 2. <option 2>
> 3. Other approach
> 
> What would you like to do?
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Keep going through tasks until done or blocked
> - Always read context files before starting (from the apply instructions output)
> - If task is ambiguous, pause and ask before implementing
> - If implementation reveals issues, pause and suggest artifact updates
> - Keep code changes minimal and scoped to each task
> - Update task checkbox immediately after completing each task
> - Pause on errors, blockers, or unclear requirements - don't guess
> - Use contextFiles from CLI output, don't assume specific file names
> 
> **Fluid Workflow Integration**
> 
> This skill supports the "actions on a change" model:
> 
> - **Can be invoked anytime**: Before all artifacts are done (if tasks exist), after partial implementation, interleaved with other actions
> - **Allows artifact updates**: If implementation reveals design issues, suggest updating artifacts - not phase-locked, work fluidly

### `2026-03-17T06:46:43.561Z`

> ---
>   Problem: pane-test-vm build crashes the nix-darwin linux-builder
> 
>   The nix build .#nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm.config.system.build.vm command consistently crashes the
>   linux-builder's nix daemon, corrupting its SQLite cache at /root/.cache/nix/binary-cache-v7.sqlite.
> 
>   Root cause: The host runs Lix (via ~/.config/nix's nix.package = pkgs.lix). Lix produces .drv files in a
>   format that diverges from CppNix. The pane VM's NixOS closure includes nix-2.31.3 (CppNix) as part of its
>   system config (the default nix.package for NixOS). When the host sends nix-2.31.3.drv to the builder, the
>   builder's CppNix daemon can't parse it, crashes, and corrupts its binary cache SQLite file.
> 
>   The nix.conf.drv for the pane VM depends on nix-2.31.3.drv:
>   /nix/store/p6w70dnqskdi0vdjdjyjsw5nfibj2g9l-nix.conf.drv
>     → /nix/store/2y1b2vr8djsv5wywwk1x31mgp6rjwydz-nix-2.31.3.drv
> 
>   This same .drv parsing incompatibility was confirmed during the nix-config builder work — nix-2.31.3.drv
>   starts with valid Derive([... content but uses Lix-specific format extensions that CppNix cannot parse.
> 
>   Why the nix-config rebuild succeeds: The builder's own NixOS config doesn't include a new nix package (it
>   uses whatever was already deployed), so nix-2.31.3.drv is never sent to the builder.
> 
>   Fix: In nix/vm.nix, add nix.package = pkgs.lix; to the pane-test-vm NixOS config. This avoids building
>   CppNix entirely — the VM will use Lix instead, and the Lix package is available from cache.lix.systems
>   (already configured as a substituter on the builder). Also add the lix cache as a substituter in the VM's
>   nix config so the VM itself can fetch lix:
> 
>   nix.package = pkgs.lix;
> 
>   After fixing, the builder's SQLite cache needs to be wiped before retrying:
>   sudo launchctl bootout system/org.nixos.linux-builder
>   sudo rm -rf /var/lib/linux-builder
>   sudo launchctl bootstrap system /Library/LaunchDaemons/org.nixos.linux-builder.plist
> 
>   Wait ~15 seconds for the VM to boot, then:
>   nix build .#nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm.config.system.build.vm
> 
>   Files to modify:
>   - nix/vm.nix — add nix.package = pkgs.lix; in the config set
> 
>   ---
>   Want me to also wipe the builder now so it's ready when your agent makes the fix

### `2026-03-17T06:46:45.417Z`

> [interrupted]

### `2026-03-17T06:46:52.970Z`

> ---
>   Problem: pane-test-vm build crashes the nix-darwin linux-builder
> 
>   The nix build .#nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm.config.system.build.vm command consistently crashes the
>   linux-builder's nix daemon, corrupting its SQLite cache at /root/.cache/nix/binary-cache-v7.sqlite.
> 
>   Root cause: The host runs Lix (via ~/.config/nix's nix.package = pkgs.lix). Lix produces .drv files in a
>   format that diverges from CppNix. The pane VM's NixOS closure includes nix-2.31.3 (CppNix) as part of its
>   system config (the default nix.package for NixOS). When the host sends nix-2.31.3.drv to the builder, the
>   builder's CppNix daemon can't parse it, crashes, and corrupts its binary cache SQLite file.
> 
>   The nix.conf.drv for the pane VM depends on nix-2.31.3.drv:
>   /nix/store/p6w70dnqskdi0vdjdjyjsw5nfibj2g9l-nix.conf.drv
>     → /nix/store/2y1b2vr8djsv5wywwk1x31mgp6rjwydz-nix-2.31.3.drv
> 
>   This same .drv parsing incompatibility was confirmed during the nix-config builder work — nix-2.31.3.drv
>   starts with valid Derive([... content but uses Lix-specific format extensions that CppNix cannot parse.
> 
>   Why the nix-config rebuild succeeds: The builder's own NixOS config doesn't include a new nix package (it
>   uses whatever was already deployed), so nix-2.31.3.drv is never sent to the builder.
> 
>   Fix: In nix/vm.nix, add nix.package = pkgs.lix; to the pane-test-vm NixOS config. This avoids building
>   CppNix entirely — the VM will use Lix instead, and the Lix package is available from cache.lix.systems
>   (already configured as a substituter on the builder). Also add the lix cache as a substituter in the VM's
>   nix config so the VM itself can fetch lix:
> 
>   nix.package = pkgs.lix;
> 
>   After fixing, the builder's SQLite cache needs to be wiped before retrying:
>   sudo launchctl bootout system/org.nixos.linux-builder
>   sudo rm -rf /var/lib/linux-builder
>   sudo launchctl bootstrap system /Library/LaunchDaemons/org.nixos.linux-builder.plist
> 
>   Wait ~15 seconds for the VM to boot, then:
>   nix build .#nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm.config.system.build.vm
> 
>   Files to modify:
>   - nix/vm.nix — add nix.package = pkgs.lix; in the config set

### `2026-03-17T07:13:57.327Z`

> ---
>   Task: Fix pane-test-vm build — Lix/CppNix derivation format incompatibility
> 
>   The host runs Lix. The linux-builder runs CppNix. When building nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm, the NixOS
>    closure includes nix-2.31.3 (CppNix) by default. The host's Lix produces a .drv file for CppNix that the
>   builder's CppNix daemon cannot parse, causing it to crash and corrupt its SQLite cache.
> 
>   Fix: Add nix.package = pkgs.lix; to the pane-test-vm NixOS config in nix/vm.nix. This replaces CppNix with
>   Lix in the VM's closure, avoiding the problematic derivation entirely. Lix is available from
>   cache.lix.systems which is already configured as a substituter on the builder.
> 
>   In nix/vm.nix, add to the config set (after system.stateVersion):
> 
>   nix.package = pkgs.lix;
> 
>   Do not add Lix to the linux-builder itself — the builder runs CppNix and that's fine. The fix is in the
>   target VM config only.
> 
>   Test after fixing:
> 
>   cd ~/src/lin/pane
>   nix build .#nixosConfigurations.pane-test-vm.config.system.build.vm
> 
>   ---

### `2026-03-17T11:52:39.473Z`

> lets look at: 1. https://github.com/phaer/nixos-vm-on-macos — uses vfkit (Apple Virtualization.framework, not QEMU) with
>   virtiofs for sharing. virtiofs handles permissions better than 9p. But vfkit is a different VM runtime than
>    our QEMU setup.
>   2. https://github.com/jordanisaacs/kernel-development-flake — uses virtiofs with a custom init that mounts
>   host directories. This is the most relevant example — they build on the host, mount the source into a VM,
>   and iterate.

### `2026-03-17T11:52:54.825Z`

> <command-message>opsx:propose</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:propose</command-name>

### `2026-03-17T11:52:54.825Z`

> Propose a new change - create the change and generate all artifacts in one step.
> 
> I'll create a change with artifacts:
> - proposal.md (what & why)
> - design.md (how)
> - tasks.md (implementation steps)
> 
> When ready to implement, run /opsx:apply
> 
> ---
> 
> **Input**: The argument after `/opsx:propose` is the change name (kebab-case), OR a description of what the user wants to build.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no input provided, ask what they want to build**
> 
>    Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** (open-ended, no preset options) to ask:
>    > "What change do you want to work on? Describe what you want to build or fix."
> 
>    From their description, derive a kebab-case name (e.g., "add user authentication" → `add-user-auth`).
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT proceed without understanding what the user wants to build.
> 
> 2. **Create the change directory**
>    ```bash
>    openspec new change "<name>"
>    ```
>    This creates a scaffolded change at `openspec/changes/<name>/` with `.openspec.yaml`.
> 
> 3. **Get the artifact build order**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>" --json
>    ```
>    Parse the JSON to get:
>    - `applyRequires`: array of artifact IDs needed before implementation (e.g., `["tasks"]`)
>    - `artifacts`: list of all artifacts with their status and dependencies
> 
> 4. **Create artifacts in sequence until apply-ready**
> 
>    Use the **TodoWrite tool** to track progress through the artifacts.
> 
>    Loop through artifacts in dependency order (artifacts with no pending dependencies first):
> 
>    a. **For each artifact that is `ready` (dependencies satisfied)**:
>       - Get instructions:
>         ```bash
>         openspec instructions <artifact-id> --change "<name>" --json
>         ```
>       - The instructions JSON includes:
>         - `context`: Project background (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `rules`: Artifact-specific rules (constraints for you - do NOT include in output)
>         - `template`: The structure to use for your output file
>         - `instruction`: Schema-specific guidance for this artifact type
>         - `outputPath`: Where to write the artifact
>         - `dependencies`: Completed artifacts to read for context
>       - Read any completed dependency files for context
>       - Create the artifact file using `template` as the structure
>       - Apply `context` and `rules` as constraints - but do NOT copy them into the file
>       - Show brief progress: "Created <artifact-id>"
> 
>    b. **Continue until all `applyRequires` artifacts are complete**
>       - After creating each artifact, re-run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json`
>       - Check if every artifact ID in `applyRequires` has `status: "done"` in the artifacts array
>       - Stop when all `applyRequires` artifacts are done
> 
>    c. **If an artifact requires user input** (unclear context):
>       - Use **AskUserQuestion tool** to clarify
>       - Then continue with creation
> 
> 5. **Show final status**
>    ```bash
>    openspec status --change "<name>"
>    ```
> 
> **Output**
> 
> After completing all artifacts, summarize:
> - Change name and location
> - List of artifacts created with brief descriptions
> - What's ready: "All artifacts created! Ready for implementation."
> - Prompt: "Run `/opsx:apply` to start implementing."
> 
> **Artifact Creation Guidelines**
> 
> - Follow the `instruction` field from `openspec instructions` for each artifact type
> - The schema defines what each artifact should contain - follow it
> - Read dependency artifacts for context before creating new ones
> - Use `template` as the structure for your output file - fill in its sections
> - **IMPORTANT**: `context` and `rules` are constraints for YOU, not content for the file
>   - Do NOT copy `<context>`, `<rules>`, `<project_context>` blocks into the artifact
>   - These guide what you write, but should never appear in the output
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Create ALL artifacts needed for implementation (as defined by schema's `apply.requires`)
> - Always read dependency artifacts before creating a new one
> - If context is critically unclear, ask the user - but prefer making reasonable decisions to keep momentum
> - If a change with that name already exists, ask if user wants to continue it or create a new one
> - Verify each artifact file exists after writing before proceeding to next

### `2026-03-17T18:47:52.857Z`

> <command-message>opsx:archive</command-message>
> <command-name>/opsx:archive</command-name>

### `2026-03-17T18:47:52.857Z`

> Archive a completed change in the experimental workflow.
> 
> **Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:archive` (e.g., `/opsx:archive add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
> 
> **Steps**
> 
> 1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**
> 
>    Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.
> 
>    Show only active changes (not already archived).
>    Include the schema used for each change if available.
> 
>    **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.
> 
> 2. **Check artifact completion status**
> 
>    Run `openspec status --change "<name>" --json` to check artifact completion.
> 
>    Parse the JSON to understand:
>    - `schemaName`: The workflow being used
>    - `artifacts`: List of artifacts with their status (`done` or other)
> 
>    **If any artifacts are not `done`:**
>    - Display warning listing incomplete artifacts
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
> 3. **Check task completion status**
> 
>    Read the tasks file (typically `tasks.md`) to check for incomplete tasks.
> 
>    Count tasks marked with `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete).
> 
>    **If incomplete tasks found:**
>    - Display warning showing count of incomplete tasks
>    - Prompt user for confirmation to continue
>    - Proceed if user confirms
> 
>    **If no tasks file exists:** Proceed without task-related warning.
> 
> 4. **Assess delta spec sync state**
> 
>    Check for delta specs at `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`. If none exist, proceed without sync prompt.
> 
>    **If delta specs exist:**
>    - Compare each delta spec with its corresponding main spec at `openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md`
>    - Determine what changes would be applied (adds, modifications, removals, renames)
>    - Show a combined summary before prompting
> 
>    **Prompt options:**
>    - If changes needed: "Sync now (recommended)", "Archive without syncing"
>    - If already synced: "Archive now", "Sync anyway", "Cancel"
> 
>    If user chooses sync, use Task tool (subagent_type: "general-purpose", prompt: "Use Skill tool to invoke openspec-sync-specs for change '<name>'. Delta spec analysis: <include the analyzed delta spec summary>"). Proceed to archive regardless of choice.
> 
> 5. **Perform the archive**
> 
>    Create the archive directory if it doesn't exist:
>    ```bash
>    mkdir -p openspec/changes/archive
>    ```
> 
>    Generate target name using current date: `YYYY-MM-DD-<change-name>`
> 
>    **Check if target already exists:**
>    - If yes: Fail with error, suggest renaming existing archive or using different date
>    - If no: Move the change directory to archive
> 
>    ```bash
>    mv openspec/changes/<name> openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>
>    ```
> 
> 6. **Display summary**
> 
>    Show archive completion summary including:
>    - Change name
>    - Schema that was used
>    - Archive location
>    - Spec sync status (synced / sync skipped / no delta specs)
>    - Note about any warnings (incomplete artifacts/tasks)
> 
> **Output On Success**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** ✓ Synced to main specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success (No Delta Specs)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** No delta specs
> 
> All artifacts complete. All tasks complete.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Success With Warnings**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Complete (with warnings)
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Schema:** <schema-name>
> **Archived to:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> **Specs:** Sync skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> **Warnings:**
> - Archived with 2 incomplete artifacts
> - Archived with 3 incomplete tasks
> - Delta spec sync was skipped (user chose to skip)
> 
> Review the archive if this was not intentional.
> ```
> 
> **Output On Error (Archive Exists)**
> 
> ```
> ## Archive Failed
> 
> **Change:** <change-name>
> **Target:** openspec/changes/archive/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>/
> 
> Target archive directory already exists.
> 
> **Options:**
> 1. Rename the existing archive
> 2. Delete the existing archive if it's a duplicate
> 3. Wait until a different date to archive
> ```
> 
> **Guardrails**
> - Always prompt for change selection if not provided
> - Use artifact graph (openspec status --json) for completion checking
> - Don't block archive on warnings - just inform and confirm
> - Preserve .openspec.yaml when moving to archive (it moves with the directory)
> - Show clear summary of what happened
> - If sync is requested, use the Skill tool to invoke `openspec-sync-specs` (agent-driven)
> - If delta specs exist, always run the sync assessment and show the combined summary before prompting
